(Part 1)

(Part 2)
Ad Hoc Committee on Gen Mkhwanazi's Allegations
The Ad Hoc Committee to Investigate Allegations made by Lieutenant General Nhlanhla Mkhwanazi met to discuss the submission of oral evidence by Mr Oupa Brown Mogotsi.
The Ad Hoc Committee to Investigate Allegations made by Nhlanhla Mkhwanazi convened to consider the oral evidence presented by Mr Oupa Brown Mogotsi.
During the proceedings, the Committee raised substantial concerns regarding the credibility of the witness’s claim that he served as a Crime Intelligence contact agent. Members questioned the absence of verifiable records confirming his status, as well as the existence of affidavits contradicting his assertion of registration. The witness attributed the lack of documentation to manual administrative processes and operational secrecy maintained by handlers; however, the Committee noted that these explanations were not supported by documentary proof. Further uncertainty arose regarding the distinction between informants, contact agents, and undercover agents. Members requested clarification on registration procedures, payment mechanisms, and the allocation of force numbers, emphasising that no audit trail or independent verification existed for the cash payments he alleged to have received.
The Committee also interrogated the basis on which the witness presented certain suspicions as factual statements in his written submission. These included claims suggesting possible involvement of the Central Intelligence Agency in matters relating to Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi and Misuzulu kaZwelithini. Under questioning, the witness acknowledged that these assertions were not supported by corroborating evidence and subsequently retracted them under oath.
Further discussion focused on the witness’s interactions with businessman Mr “Cat” Matlala. Although the witness stated that he had been investigating Matlala for alleged tender irregularities and possible links to the “Big Five”, the Committee expressed concern that he had simultaneously accepted payments and logistical assistance from the same individual. Members questioned whether this conduct constituted legitimate infiltration or suggested possible collaboration or extortion.
The Committee also examined operational claims relating to alleged undercover activities, including references to recordings under Section 252A of the Criminal Procedure Act concerning a purported plot against General Khan. Members raised concerns about the use of fabricated identities reportedly linked to the Minister’s office as part of “legend-building” for the operation. The Committee noted that transcripts presented during the proceedings implicated several senior officials but had not been independently verified by the witness.
Additional inconsistencies were highlighted. These included assertions that the witness had conducted surveillance at his own expense, obtained intelligence from Uber drivers, and accessed occurrence book entries without statutory authority. Members questioned whether these activities complied with the provisions of National Instruction 2 of 2001, which governs the management of handlers and intelligence agents within the South African Police Service.
The Committee also expressed concern regarding the witness’s legal history, referencing previous cases involving murder—later framed as culpable homicide—assault, fraud, and various driving offences. Members questioned how an individual with such a background could have been entrusted with sensitive tasks, including travel to Kenya and alleged involvement in matters connected to the Political Killings Task Team. The witness’s claims of harassment were also scrutinised due to the absence of case numbers or supporting documentation.
Further queries related to the witness’s alleged role in the CR17 campaign associated with Cyril Ramaphosa, his communications with the President, and his purported connections to Senzo Mchunu. Members questioned whether these relationships may have influenced his motivations, raising concerns about potential bias rather than objective intelligence gathering.
In conclusion, the Committee emphasised that its assessment of the allegations concerning misconduct within the South African Police Service would depend on the submission of tangible evidence, including documentation confirming the witness’s status, details of his handlers, and institutional verification of the operations he described. The witness undertook to provide additional materials to support his claims.

These include, among others, the alleged unlawful disbandment of the Political Killings Task Team, the alleged moratorium on the filling of vacancies within the South African Police Service, and the alleged corrupt relationship between senior leadership within the SAPS and members of the public, as well as political interference in the work of the SAPS.
In extending this invitation, the Ad Hoc Committee Chairperson has indicated that you may provide such information to the Committee, if you so wish, under oath in terms of the Powers, Privileges and Immunities of Parliament. Please be informed that by law you are required to answer fully and satisfactorily all the questions lawfully put to you, or to produce any document that you are required to produce in connection with the subject matter of the enquiry, notwithstanding the fact that the answer or the document could incriminate you or expose you to criminal or civil proceedings or damages.
You are, however, protected in that evidence given under oath or affirmation before a House or Committee may not be used against you in any court or place outside Parliament, except in criminal proceedings concerning a charge of perjury or a charge relating to evidence or documents required in the proceedings.
Please be aware that in terms of section 17(2) of the Powers, Privileges and Immunities of Parliament and Provincial Legislatures Act, a person who wilfully furnishes a House or Committee with information, or makes a statement before it which is false or misleading, commits an offence and is liable to a fine or to imprisonment for a period not exceeding two years.

Should I only speak to what I am doing now as a small businessman, or does your question also include the part on Crime Intelligence, or the whole paragraph?

Mr Mogotsi: Okay. As a businessman, I am running a few businesses, including food production in terms of beef and so forth. Going to the Crime Intelligence part, as you say, any position. I became an informant of Crime Intelligence back in the 1990s, in 1999.
And I also became an informant of the hotel. I think you must drag your chair towards the mic. You are sitting too far away; that is why you are far from the mic. Yes, I think so far it is reaching. This is the status where I am now.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So you say that over the years you have been involved in Crime Intelligence as an informant, and you worked as a Crime Intelligence agent. Are you currently still a Crime Intelligence agent?
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: How long have you been a Crime Intelligence agent?
Mr Mogotsi: By virtue of becoming a contact agent, perhaps I should say that as an informant I served for a number of years. You now ask about an agent. That was in 2009. That is when I became an agent.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: You deal with some of this in your statement, in your background, where you explain from paragraph 13 onwards. But what is not apparent from your explanation is exactly when you were registered and how. You say, “During 2009, I was registered and acted as an agent for Crime Intelligence in the police services.” Can you elaborate on that? The reason I ask is that you would note, and this was also referred to you in the Madlanga Commission, that affidavits were produced by individuals stating that you were not in Crime Intelligence. Could you explain why they would say that and take us through your registration process?
Mr Mogotsi: As an informant, that was in 2001. I then did some operations as an informant from 2001. In 2003, I was deregistered as I was no longer active. When I became an agent, that is when I was recruited. That is the difference between an informant and a contact agent. That is how I got recruited and given some small tasks and information that I used to provide. They would say go back, they would give me a file to note, submit, and so forth. The only difference here is that a contact agent will not have any identity of some sort. You only work with your handler. He will give you the task and you report back to him, and so forth.
In relation to the affidavits that you are referring to that were brought to Madlanga, they were not ventilated at Madlanga. However, I think I now have the opportunity to speak to that. I do not know if I should refer Members to the affidavits the evidence leader is referring to.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: This is annexure “BM2” of your annexure bundle. It starts on page 5 to page 9. Those are the two affidavits from members who are part of Crime Intelligence who say that you were not registered as a Crime Intelligence member.
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct. The affidavit, I know the name of the Colonel who wrote it. He was in the admin support staff of the South African Police Service. If you check his affidavit, he only became the acting head of the agents programme in 2024. He definitely would not know me. Even if he were asked about three or four different contacts, he would not know them.
This is supported in his affidavit. If you check on page 5, paragraph stating “I am a police officer”, the next one says “Mr Brown’s identity has never been in our programme”. However, if we go to the next affidavit, there is another affidavit on page 8 from the same Crime Intelligence division. Paragraph 5 going down says “The ID number belonging to Mr Brown Mogotsi was tested against the CI database. The ID numbers registered in the Capfin (spelling unconfirmed) and a source was handled by and co-handled by, and the particular amount of money was given”.
Now those are two contradictory affidavits coming from the same division of Crime Intelligence. It is only perhaps a submission of these particular handlers and co-handlers, whom I mentioned here, who will be able to attest to my registration.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: In paragraph 15 of your statement, you say that the individuals who deposed to these affidavits are newly appointed to Crime Intelligence and that they were asked to fabricate the facts stated in the affidavit in order to discredit you. I would like to go back to one of those statements, the last one you just read. The second individual who deposed to the statement has been in Crime Intelligence since 2015, so that does not seem to be a newly appointed member in Crime Intelligence. On page 7, it is stated, “I have been stationed at the Secret Service Account Division, Crime Intelligence, since 2015.” That goes against what you said in your statement.
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So this is not somebody new.
Mr Mogotsi: I do not see the difference now. Oh, this is the second affidavit. Yes. What is the question?
Adv Mokhoaetsi: My question is this. I read paragraph 15 of your statement, where you said these individuals are newly appointed. You read the first statement that said the person was appointed in 2024. The second individual says that he has been at Crime Intelligence since 2015. So that is not a newly appointed person. Do you agree?
Mr Mogotsi: Yes, but being appointed in that division in 2015 may have interacted with my other projects and assignments between those years until 2021, I believe.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: What does that mean?
Mr Mogotsi: I am saying if a person was appointed in 2015, and I became a contact agent in 2009, he may have interacted with my assignments, that particular person, unlike the one who was appointed in 2024 and says he does not know me. Obviously, there is no way he could know me. I am saying in this affidavit that if you check, the first one is talking about fabrication. The particular Colonel was appointed by Lieutenant General Lushaba in the finance section. This person, the same one in 2024, who says I am not appearing on the system, whereas there is one that says there is a Capfin number and so forth. This one, who was appointed in 2015, was actually appointed by Lieutenant General Lushaba in 2024.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Let us go to what the second person says about your registration in 2009. The second individual on page 8 of his statement says that the source was registered in 2001, on 9 January, I believe, at Soweto Cluster. In the same statement, it says the source was deregistered in 2001. So this person suggests that you were only in Crime Intelligence for a couple of months. It then says the handlers requested an amount of R1 200 as a recruitment fee to motivate the contact. According to their report, there are no other financial transactions related to the source for the period you were active in the system. So he says you were only active for a couple of months in 2001.
Mr Mogotsi: Yes, that is correct. That is what he is saying. You see here, if you check it properly, he is talking about when I was registered as an informant. Now those are two different things. Here, he is referring to me when I was an informant. When I became a contact agent, the registration is not done in the same way as this one. It is done manually, and the file is kept by your handler. All your transactions, how you get reimbursed, assisted or paid, are done through cash from your handler all the time. So an informant and a contact agent are not processed in the same way.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Why is that explanation not in your statement? Why do we only know that these people have been asked to fabricate and that they are newly appointed? It seems that what you are saying is that even if they have been in Crime Intelligence for however many years, they would not have been able to trace you on the system. But that explanation is not what you have given in your statement.
Mr Mogotsi: Maybe I should give a background about this process. The way informants and agents are eliminated, I am not the only one who was registered and deregistered in a very short period of time. It is when your life is in danger that your handler decides to register you in a manner that will not be visible in the system. If you see part of my statement, I am talking about an informant who was murdered simply because they could not trace the informant. They did not have his contact details. They had to get one Brigadier to go with a handler to meet the informant and give him that R50 000.
That informant is not on the system, but look, his payment was processed. I am trying to say that, depending on the work and the operation you do, not everyone will appear on a particular database. If you look at these databases, they are referring to two different things. In this registration, we are talking about an informant. In the first affidavit, he is talking about an SSA Central Informant Index. He is talking about an undercover agent in that affidavit. “Brown Mogotsi’s ID being in our programme as an undercover project,” he says, “has never been in our programme as an undercover agent”.
Now, a contact agent and an undercover agent are two different people. Undercover agents are police. You will be surprised that they do not get paid through the bank. They do not have PERSAL numbers, but they are police. So he is referring to that. I am saying wherever he is, he does not know the difference.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So what were you? What was your position?
Mr Mogotsi: A contact agent.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: A contact agent, which is different from an undercover agent.
Mr Mogotsi: Very different, in the sense that undercover agents are usually police officers.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: If all of this, as I have indicated, your explanation is that you would have been missed because of how the registration is done, why are you saying in your statement that these individuals were instructed by General Khumalo and General Lushaba to fabricate facts about you?
Mr Mogotsi: I will speak shortly about General Lushaba. It is in the statement. When he had a female friend at his house in the morning, they stayed together, and in the morning, the cell phone and the laptops were gone. In realising that the phones and the state’s property were not there, he went and opened a case of housebreaking. Just to correct something, it is written as “Brooklyn”, but it was actually in Villieria. In the particular case, the lady could not be found.
Then, Major General Lushaba, I do not know how the information leaked, because the officer from Crime Intelligence who was assisting in compiling and gathering information realised that this was actually not housebreaking but perjury. This Major General lied. He ended up being sidelined and fired because there was never a case. Now General Lushaba knows me. You should check that the case was opened here in Cape Town against Major General Lushaba.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Mr Mogotsi, you deal with that extensively in your statement, and I want you to take us carefully through it when we reach that part. But I do not want it to get mixed up with your explanation as to why you say General Lushaba and General Khumalo fabricated facts about you. Can we deal with that aspect first?
Mr Mogotsi: Yes. I am saying that the only way you could do that is to get someone to say that he does not know me. Part of this investigation led to him knowing that we realised that this was not housebreaking. And how does Lieutenant General Khumalo come in? I am saying that because he is the head, the Divisional Head of Crime Intelligence. It is surprising. Even one of the journalists asked me how a Lieutenant General, a Divisional Commissioner, does not know you, whereas you claim to be whatever. I am saying he had to deal with Major General Lushaba to ensure that they discredit me. They even say they do not know about me. That is where the fabrication comes from.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Let me turn to “BM1” of your annexure bundle, which is page 1. There is an affidavit that you deposed to. Could you explain to us what the purpose of that affidavit was?
Mr Mogotsi: Yes. Firstly, on the page that I requested, I will repeat the request. There are names of officers mentioned there, and I have requested that, as I speak about that, I would request not to mention their names.
Acting Chairperson: Is that the reason why their names have been affected in the annexure bundle?
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct. In fact, the agreement was that they were going to be redacted. Now, on the circling, it was probably the evidence leader directing the person who was doing that work, and the person could not redact those names correctly. But that is the reason. Those names that are circled should not be mentioned.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Just for clarity, we were trying to redact the names, but it seems the printers made a mistake. Mr Mogotsi has confirmed that if it stays within the House, it would be fine to make it available in the way that it currently is.
Acting Chairperson: So, there was general consensus between you and the witness on the usage of this information?
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Yes.
Mr J Malema (EFF): I think we are moving a bit fast because I thought we were still at the introduction level, where there are three issues that have not been answered. The first one is why Mr Mogotsi is calling himself an entrepreneur. I want to understand that because it cannot just be a concept loosely thrown around. Secondly, what is an informant? Under which department does an informant fall? And what is an agent? Under which department does that fall? And between the informant and the agent, which one has a force number, not PERSAL, that we are able to account for when paying this particular agent? Because that clarity is not coming out, and I think we need to get that clarity. Then we know whether we are dealing with an entrepreneur, if he is one, an informant, if he is one, or an agent, if he is one.
Acting Chairperson: The first issue is the issue of the names. I think if there is consensus that the usage of the names must be avoided wherever possible, that should be observed. Mr Mogotsi, I was also tempted, like Mr Malema, to enter on the issue of the informant, the contact agent and the undercover agent. So I think you must also give us the significant difference between the three. You should also address the point that when you introduced yourself in your sworn statement, you said, “I am an entrepreneur.” Perhaps you can take us through that. You may proceed. Let us allow him to first deal with this matter, and then we will come to you, Mr Skosana.
Mr Mogotsi: The question of an entrepreneur may be understood in different ways. I only call myself an entrepreneur because I am selling. I have a small business, and sometimes we apply for entrepreneur development programmes with SEDA. We make those applications, and that is how I put it, that I am an entrepreneur.
Probably Mr Malema and others may say no, because you are selling on a small scale, you are this or that. I may not be able to give it in the proper way in which it is understood, but I just call myself a small business entrepreneur. To me, they sound the same.
Mr Malema: Before you go there, you are saying you are selling. What are you selling? Where?
Mr Mogotsi: I have some liquor outlets. I also sell and distribute meat and manufacture wors and other products for different events such as funerals, weddings and so forth. Most importantly, I do a lot of catering, food for events and so forth. None of this comes from the government, by the way. It is only a private business. I deal with private businesses.
Acting Chairperson: So you have an abattoir?
Mr Mogotsi: No, not an abattoir. I buy from the abattoir.
Acting Chairperson: You can proceed on the significant differences between the informant, the contact agent and the undercover agent.
Mr Mogotsi: Thank you, Chair. Perhaps I should give a proper explanation. I will give an example. If three people go and steal somewhere and one gets arrested while the other two run away, the one who is arrested may make a deal with the police and say that after stealing here, they are planning to steal somewhere else. The information he provides to the police means that at that moment, the police may decide that he becomes their informant. They then go and trace the others, and if a crime takes place and they manage to arrest them, that person is declared an informant.
Another way is that an informant can come from anywhere, even from Parliament, working here. If there is anything going on that is not correct, the moment he gives that information he becomes an informant.
In many cases, the police officer, especially in the detective section, will realise that a particular person is always in town and knows people who are selling drugs or something similar. They may feel that they can work with him and that he can give them information as and when needed. Then they make him an informant.
The contact agent, on the other hand, will not appear in that system. He has a relationship with the handler. The handler brings an assignment and says there is certain information and asks whether he can work on it. The moment you are registered by a Crime Intelligence officer, you start identifying individuals in different ranks, perhaps in government departments and institutions, with whom you work. Those individuals then become your informants, and you build a network of informants who give you information, which you then give to your handler.
For example, an informant does not have a file. He simply gives the police information, and they act on it. But for a contact agent, there is a file where he writes reports. When you get an assignment, the handler will go to his commanders, make arrangements and get permission for the operation. If there is a controlled intelligence transaction that will take place, the handler informs the police of that place before it happens, and that is when the police act.
I do not know if I am understood. I was going to give an example using BM1, this affidavit that is written here. This affidavit came from a source. The source made me meet with a colonel who was aware of a disciplinary hearing that was to take place. This colonel was one of the witnesses. He was called together and given a mandate on how to fabricate stories to favour the employer and to get a particular general expelled.
In that sense, I had to speak to my handler. The handler arranged with the DPCI, and we requested permission to conduct an operation in terms of section 252A, where you request in advance to conduct a trap or operation. We recorded this colonel. He gave information about the plot and how they were going to dismiss a particular general.
After recording this colonel, we were able to depose to an affidavit. A case was opened by the DPCI and the investigating officer took the matter. I do not know how far the case has gone.
To be precise, the same recording and this affidavit were used in the Madlanga Commission, where I was told that I was a liar and a professional liar. It is because the same police officer could not trap me. I had to give him the impression that if he gave me the information, he might get a promotion or some other benefit. I told him that I was working with the Minister of Police and that the matter would be handled. Indeed, he cooperated, and I managed to record him. The audio is there, and the transcripts are available for Members to look at.
Most significantly, after Madlanga, the same recording was used to charge this police officer. He was served with a document to appear at a disciplinary hearing. I am trying to show that, as an agent, you are able to conduct an operation. An informant could not apply for section 252A, but an agent can speak to the handler and request it. That is the difference.
Continuation of leading evidence by the evidence leader
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Just to go back to my question, and I think Mr Mogotsi touched on BM1. Could you explain what the purpose of this affidavit was and who it went to after you deposed to it?
Mr Mogotsi: It went to Lieutenant Colonel Schnelle from the DPCI. In fact, it is on page four where he signed and acknowledged it. I spoke about this affidavit. The names I was referring to earlier are not those that I am mentioning now. This colonel was called in KZN by the employer at that time, Major General Khumalo, who told him how to fabricate the story. He also mentioned that Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi knew about it and that Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi was going to preside over the matter, and that Lieutenant General Khumalo also knew.
That is the recording I have in the transcripts. We took this to the DPCI, and a case was opened. I am trying to show that as an agent, you are able to conduct an operation which can be registered with the DPCI or any other department.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So I am still trying to clarify the purpose of this affidavit, and I will explain why. Are you saying that this affidavit was deposed to in your capacity as a contact agent in order to get an operation authorised?
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: In paragraph 1 of this affidavit that you deposed to, you describe yourself as a male employed in government with the office of the Minister. Is that the title you carry as a contact agent?
Mr Mogotsi: No, you will not carry one title. Maybe as an agent, there comes another important thing. One is subjected to something called legend building. Legend building is an instrument that is utilised all over the world by international Crime Intelligence services. As a legend builder, you create a false life to attain the objective, provided your handler knows of the operation.
You see, I said if I did not say to this man that I was with the Minister of Police, there would have been no reason for him to trust me and give me that information. But by virtue of promising him that with this information, I would try to assist him, because he wanted a promotion, I promised him. This was done and explained in my affidavit, as he wanted. It also matches what reflects on the transcript and the recording.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So, who approved the 252A?
Mr Mogotsi: Lieutenant Colonel Schnelle.
Acting Chairperson: Adv Mokhoaetsi, can we stay on BM1?
Adv Mokhoaetsi: It is BM1.
Acting Chairperson: Paragraph 1. There is an ID number reflected there. The witness must confirm if that is his ID number. There is also a cell phone contact there. I think you must confirm that as well.
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct. I just want to give an explanation because this also raised concern in Madlanga. This is my ID number. This is the current ID number that I will carry for my life unless, with the application that I made with the BI-212 at Home Affairs, they are able to rectify my date of birth.
That is why in Madlanga they said you were 13 years old in 1979, and it is in the statement. I am trying to clarify that when I applied for an ID, the number came out incorrect. There is no way I can say that I do not want this ID number or that I cannot use it. It is there. It is my ID number. In everything that I do, this is my ID number.
You cannot put the wrong ID number because you are using legend building or something similar. You have to produce the ID. The Commissioner of Oaths must look at your ID and confirm that this is indeed your ID number. That is the ID number that I have.
For information, even though I come from another area, there is one person younger than me whose ID was incorrectly captured at Home Affairs and recorded as 1951. Today, he is receiving a pension because of the problem at Home Affairs.
It is unfortunate that when this affidavit and the 252A operation were used, the state was able to rely on it to charge this police officer. In Madlanga, they felt that I lied and therefore I was a professional liar, whereas it was being utilised to attain the state objective of charging the police officer.

Acting Chairperson: That is noted. I think the evidence leader was proceeding along that line earlier. You may proceed with the evidence leader, and Mr Mogotsi will respond as guided.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Just to add to what has been asked about the reference to being employed in the office of the Minister, and the lack of clarity about where this affidavit was going and its exact purpose. If one looks at BM3, where Colonel Schnelle refers to “Mr Mogotsi”, not referring to the statement but referring to you as the complainant, he also refers to you as someone who is a politician deployed to the office of Minister Mchunu.
He says this is the basis on which he is making the application, not you. From his statement, it looks like he is the one making the application. He refers to you as the complainant and says that you are a politician deployed to the office of the Minister, which is what you described yourself as in BM1.
So I am trying to understand whether you deposed to BM1 as a complainant, to be used by someone who is actually an intelligence officer to apply for a 252A, or whether you were the intelligence officer applying for the 252A. Because if you look further, and just to add before you answer, in paragraph 7 on page 12 he says: “I will be applying for a section 252A authority for the operation to take place.” It therefore seems that you are simply the complainant.
Mr Mogotsi: For one to apply for 252A, which is for trapping and similar operations done by the DPCI, the officer in the DPCI must complete the form. I cannot go to a DPCI officer and say that I am an agent and that I am going to lie to someone that he will get a promotion. There is no way you can do that.
You go to him and say where you are employed. You can see there is another person I was with. He is also a colonel. He was relying on me to assist him with what he wanted. Then he would give us the information he was talking about.
The 252A, including a section 205 application, and other legal documents, can only be applied for by the police. In this case it is done by the DPCI because they administer the traps. For example, when you want to trap someone and obtain money from them, they complete the forms and obtain authority to do that particular action.
If you read the documents, you will see that authority must be obtained before carrying out the operation. This is a good question. For example, any agent can never bring you evidence. We deal with information. I do not obtain statements from people. I cannot come to you and say that I am an agent and ask you to write a statement.
Throughout my statement you will see that I mentioned people such as Prince Zulu from KZN who had a problem. He was brought to Gauteng and we helped him open a case. But the police must take him through the process to open a case. Even if I am involved, the police must still process it. I cannot obtain a statement.
Even today, there will be evidence presented, but I cannot produce evidence. I can only provide information and indicate who can corroborate that information. Once it is corroborated, it becomes the evidence that you require.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Mr Mogotsi, who did you lie to here? Who was the person you needed to lie to in order to have the 252A approved? You appear to be dealing with people who are part of the DPCI and part of the trap operation. So, who did you lie to when you made that application?
Mr Mogotsi: You first record a person and then request authority. That means I was operating two people: Colonel Schnelle and the colonel I was recording.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: The affidavit that you deposed to, my question is, who did you want to obtain approval from? Was it from Schnelle?
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.

Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.

Mr Mogotsi: It was then submitted. I believe you must look at the outcome and whether it worked or not. The moment we recorded the person and obtained the document, it means the objective was achieved.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Who approved it?

Adv Mokhoaetsi: What then subsequently happened after the approval of the 252A?
Mr Mogotsi: I recorded the person, submitted the recording and obtained the transcript. My job was done. It was then up to Colonel Schnelle to decide what to do with the case.
Also, regarding the Madlanga reference you made earlier, Commissioner Madlanga referred to your statement and said that you were lying when he referred to your ID number. However, you have not provided any proof to show otherwise.
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct, Chair. You see how the 1979 and 1977 came about. It was one of the Commissioners in Madlanga who thought that I said I was from uMkhonto weSizwe and that I was a member or soldier. He said that even if I were a soldier, would I have been a soldier at the age of 13?
I explained to him that when I was in the SDU it was not at the age of 13. I was turning 15. I was 15 years old because I was not born in 1977. By the way, in these SDUs, there were people younger than 13, even 12. I was not trying to prove that I was a soldier in uMkhonto weSizwe.
Perhaps if I had not spoken about it and simply said that I was 13 but that I was not in uMkhonto weSizwe, that it was an SDU, we would not be having this discussion about the ID and the date of birth. I raised it to clarify that I was not in uMkhonto weSizwe, but that I was also not 13 years old.
With regard to proof, in those years, you would have had a baptismal certificate. Many of those churches closed down, and I cannot go and make a new baptismal certificate now. That would be another lie if I were to bring a certificate that was issued last week or last month. I looked for the old priests, but most of them are no longer alive.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Just to go back before we move on, on your allegations of being a Crime Intelligence contact agent. Adv Mokhoaetsi: How would this Committee be able to be satisfied that you were, in fact, a Crime Intelligence contact agent? Mr Mogotsi: I would be dead. If one operation comes and I say I am this, there is no way you can survive, there is no way. That is why I am happy Members were saying it is not jump. Adv Mokhoaetsi: No, Mr Mogotsi, maybe you can explain to us. It seems that you are willing to expose classified information and talk about classified information. Mr Mogotsi: Yes. The co-handler is going to appear; he is being summoned to the Madlanga Commission. Who knew my handler? Mr Mogotsi: You will be surprised that out of the investigation there was, or there still is, as we speak, a flat rate payment for informants of R3 000. That is how the rate of drugs and crime went up, because the informants were under-reimbursed with a very small amount. It was a flat rate. Now it was one of the first things that I picked up, that in Crime Intelligence this is the problem. With Crime Intelligence, we gather any information that has to do with crime. And it is true that it was known that General Mfazi passed on due to COVID and so forth. And his body was exhumed twice. That is when there was that lead that he was poisoned. The investigation is still there.

And in this intelligence circle, you will have one brigadier, maybe in the Eastern Cape, who has the knowledge and who will refer a person to another brigadier in Gauteng, and stuff like that. So they were referred to open a case. That is why the case was immediately transferred to KZN.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: It is not something that you picked up during your investigations into him being a CIA agent that led you to become involved in this? This is completely not related.
Mr Mogotsi: No, it is the handler who brings the information to say another person in Nongoma; they are sending people here to come and open a case, because the cases cannot be opened in KZN.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So, in paragraph 36, you mentioned that you travelled to Kenya. You also just stated that you have attached a copy of your passport or provided us with a copy of your passport that confirms that you did, in fact, travel to Kenya. And we have attached it to the bundle, in the annexure bundle. It is not numbered, but it is at the very end of the annexure bundle, the last two pages, I believe. Members will see there is a copy of Mr Mogotsi’s passport that indicates the extent of his travels on the 10th and the 11th of September.
So, just before we move on to the next issue, is there anything in relation to the outcome of your travels that you would like to put on record, your discussions with George that confirmed your suspicions about Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi?
Mr Mogotsi: Yes. As things stand now, I can never say indeed the suspicions are correct, because after I briefed the late former Minister, who also spoke of him coming to Madlanga at that time, and that George, he has knowledge about these operations of the CIA in Southern Africa, but he could not give me something tangible to produce.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Now, in paragraph 38 of your statement, you speak of Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi, and you say that you have learned that not all his suspects make it out alive, and they are basically denied the right to a fair trial. Now that is a very serious allegation, but it is not quite clear what you mean by that. Do you want to elaborate on what you mean?
Mr Mogotsi: It is not that I learned. Everyone knows what happened in KZN. Every time people were there, they were fighting back with the police, and they never came back alive. Every time. And I do not say they must shoot the police. But in that shooting, you never find one police officer who has been shot in the head or something. Every time the suspect does not get a fair trial to appear in court. That is my point.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: In your statement, it seems to suggest something stronger. It says that I came to learn that all Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi’s suspects did not make it out alive. You are saying that every person he arrests does not make it out alive, and does not get a chance to have a fair trial?
Mr Mogotsi: I think one of the reasons crime cannot go down in many instances is that where there is the death penalty in certain countries, people do go to court, have a fair trial, are found guilty, convicted and sentenced. In a scenario where every time the criminals, and I am not saying these criminals must go and do all these things, I am just saying they should be arrested and appear before the court.
And you cannot have a democracy where every time, as if the crime in the Western Cape does happen, in the Northern Cape, in many places, suspects do get arrested. Others get away, get identified and get arrested. But for these people, they will not. Every time. And they do not get a chance to shoot back. I do not say they must shoot back. I am just saying there is never evidence to know where these criminals come from, because they get killed before they can reveal who is sending them, or the big people behind them.
Acting Chairperson: But you, in paragraph 37, are making reference to a series of events that you conducted with former Minister Mthethwa, who died under suspicious circumstances. And the following paragraph is the one that says you have learned that suspects of Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi do not make it out alive. And you will recall that just recently, you made an allegation of Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi having worked for the CIA. So what is the relationship between these statements?
Mr Mogotsi: No. Minister Mthethwa was not Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi’s suspect. He was never his suspect. And the suspicious circumstances I was referring to were even here in Cape Town. From the second floor or the third floor, it is impossible to open that window with a scissor. They are very strong. I was just talking about my own view as to how it is possible to break it. It is unlike this one in the hall. If you go to hotels, you can check, but you can never open that glass and fall from there. It was my thinking. I was still thinking the same.
But it has nothing to do with Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi’s matter. It is just that, because again I was referring to his suspects, or the suspects mostly based in KZN, who usually get into fights with the police.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: And also, maybe just to go a little bit back, I think I skipped a very important part of your statement, which is from paragraph 31 onwards, paragraph 31 and paragraph 32. You referred to Mr Matlala’s engagement with Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi, and you say that Mr Matlala reminded you just prior to, sorry, when Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi had his press statement or press conference, Mr Matlala reminded you that he previously made reference to travelling to Durban in order to meet a person who could solve all his difficulties.
Do you want to explain what difficulties Mr Matlala had and talk about the alleged meeting between himself and Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi?
Mr Mogotsi: Usually, when you know a person, you will not know all his problems, and he will probably say I have problems. But the day he says, you know there is this important person in KZN and this meeting that I have to attend, and should that materialise I think my problems will be solved, that is what happened.
And there is the same evidence that I led that when I had to, because he mentioned the date, when I drove to Durban and waited, and all those things, and followed them to the place in Umhlanga. It is unfortunate that in Madlanga, one of the commissioners said Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi never said he was staying in Umhlanga. But my investigation was based on following the man and seeing where he goes, and that place was in Umhlanga.
Now the most important thing out of that meeting is that I did not see who the person was whom he met. And after some time, after he got arrested, there was a press conference of Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi. As he was speaking, from the prison cell on his phone the same day after the press conference, he did mention that, you know, my brother, do you remember the day when I told you I went to KZN? I actually went to meet Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi.
And I still maintain that, given the period of time Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi had to address the media, I believe he was supposed to take the country into confidence that he also met with Mr ‘Cat’ Matlala. During the press conference, again, he said there was a meeting arranged by Minister Senzo Mchunu, the National Commissioner, General Sibiya, and himself. And in conclusion to what you are saying, he did say he will never have a meeting with a criminal.
Now to my surprise, the alleged member of the Big Five said he met with him, corroborated by Major General Senona, who said he was just taking some drinks. It showed the environment where they were sitting, and they could even have drinks together. But he never took the country into confidence that I was actually with Mr Matlala.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: What were you doing in Durban at the time?
Mr Mogotsi: No, I travelled specifically because Mr Matlala did mention he was going to meet somebody. But I actually thought it was Mr Bheki Cele.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: What were you trying to achieve? You travelled because Mr Matlala said he was going to Durban to meet someone, and what was it to you?
Mr Mogotsi: If you check now, out of the task when dealing with Mr Matlala, it included knowing who he was working with. Who he was meeting was important.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: He also told you he gave Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi money?
Mr Mogotsi: No. He just said I gave him something. And I did try to explain to the evidence leader that he had given him something on the phone when he was talking to him.
Mr Malema: So when you say he says he does not meet criminals, following the meeting with him, General Sibiya, the Minister and the Commissioner, but he does not take the country into confidence that he met Mr Matlala and General Senona. Are you implying that Mr Matlala is a criminal in your own words?
Mr Mogotsi: It is derived from what he said. He has linked him to being one of the Big Five.
Mr Malema: No, let us leave what he said. You are saying that because he met Mr Matlala, after he told the country that he does not meet criminals, he meets Mr Matlala and then keeps quiet. He should have told us that he met a criminal, Matlala himself. So are you regarding Mr Matlala as a criminal?
Mr Mogotsi: No, I am not regarding him as a criminal.
Mr Malema: So why is that important? Why should he tell us about a meeting between a general, Mr Matlala and himself?
Mr Mogotsi: If meeting the Minister and two generals, the third one being himself, has one criminal amongst them, it definitely will apply when he meets the person who is alleged to be one of the Big Five and not just someone who steals milk or whatever. He is accused of being a member of the Big Five.
Acting Chairperson: Yes. But also, Mr Mogotsi, when you say Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi said he can never have a meeting with a criminal, are you referring to the media briefing of 6 July?
Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.

Mr Mogotsi: That is correct.

Acting Chairperson: No, I am saying you are saying he said he will never meet with a criminal. He said there can never be peace between a police officer and a criminal, referring to a meeting between himself, Minister Mchunu and General Sibiya.
Mr Mogotsi: Yes. And there you are, correct. I may have
Acting Chairperson: So, do you agree that you are quoting all this out of context?
Mr Mogotsi: That is what I believed. And it is important, the distinction you are drawing now shows that peace and meeting are not the same.
Acting Chairperson: No, but you are referring to a meeting between Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi and Mr Matlala, and you are referring to what Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi has said in the press briefing, which are two completely different things, because Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi was simply speaking about a meeting arranged by Minister Mchunu.
Mr Mogotsi: Yes.

Mr Mogotsi: I agree.
Continuation of Leading Evidence

The Cellbrite machine is the only machine which, when Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi was here, said to Members they can retrieve messages and see whatever.
So with the information I have, in SAPS there is no one who is able to use that machine. There are three companies in possession of this machine. That is Magma and these other two companies. Because of the relationship Magma has with Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi, that is where the suspicion is raised that it was actually used to, even with all these messages about Mr Matlala, among others, it is this company that has done that. That is what you are saying. So that corroboration can convert the information I have to the evidence that you want here.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: And those people that you are referring to in relation to these investigations that you have conducted, and that they would be able to come and corroborate, what are they currently doing with this information?

Mr Mogotsi: There is something that probably I can quote. I was so happy to see it being mentioned by the chairperson of the Committee about these mafias who are not dangerous but invincible because they are running government. It is a similar thing about cases which are open.
The case that led to the arrest of Lieutenant General Khumalo, Lekalakala, Leshaba and those generals, it was open two times. They could not be arrested. It was by luck that the matter was then, through a certain referral to IDAC, investigated and they were arrested. You could still ask the question, if they were able to be arrested by IDAC, why were they not arrested when the matter was open in Cape Town or Soweto? It is because somebody must say yes.
If I give you proof that a property has been bought for R22 million, it is not in the name of the state. If it is on the name, probably it was changed. But there is a title deed that shows the name of the person in whose name the property was registered. And this, where I am sitting, is the last line of defence. I believe you can call whoever and say, here is the title deed. How did you buy this property in the name of this individual?
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So you are saying, rather, that you consider the Committee the last avenue or the last sort of resort that can come in and assist. But how will it do it? Must it now call these people who will come and corroborate, whom you have not mentioned here? Will you give the names later? How is the Committee going to come to your assistance if you have not given it enough information?
Mr Mogotsi: The Committee gave me three or seven days to bring what should be corroborated to the attention of the Chairperson, including the proof that the forklift was bought for R900,000 instead of R250,000. The property of R22 million. Whatever information says there were R120 million. But I only mentioned the R22 million property evidence that was bought.
Now imagine I was with the evidence leader yesterday, but we still cannot produce it here because it is classified. Now I said, remember, I am a layman. I cannot make statements. But if the Committee feels compelled to compel whoever, probably the NPA, probably whoever, and says, here is the information. Why are you not acting? Probably something will happen.

There are cases that are being opened but not prosecuted, or they are not allowing cases to be opened. Mr Mogotsi: Yes, but remember that it is classified information. Probably, if the Committee could summon the IGI or have access to the IGI report, in whichever way that is allowed in terms of the law, then we will not talk about those things. Everything is there.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: In paragraph 40, again, you mention one of your investigations that you have done into Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi, and this is one where you say he refused to open a case against a correctional officer who was found in possession of drugs. Where is this case currently? Do you want us to, or maybe do you want to explain first how you learned of this information? Was this one of the formal operations that you participated in, or is it something that you heard about through the grapevine?
Mr Mogotsi: No, no. I remember it was I who spoke to Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi, and when he appeared here, at least he had his phone. Our phones are not in our possession. On his phone, he was able to produce my communication with him, where I sent him proof of the OB entry from Empangeni Police Station. The case was open. The officer could not be arrested because he intervened, and in his response, he explained to me exactly what happened and why he felt the officer should not be arrested, and that the drugs were found in the rubbish bin outside.
But this is not the only case which was open. I did mention a matter in Rustenburg, where there were zama zama and people with unlicensed firearms. There had been some shooting two days before the information came. Because this thing works in Rustenburg, that is when they brought in the Tactical Management Operations, TOMS, Operation Management System, or the DPCI. They came there and had to sit somewhere, and at a particular period they went into the place.
They found my security officers wearing black uniforms, with their firearms also. They demanded that each and every one produce permits and licences. The security officers produced them, and they let them go. They gave them back their ammunition, then they went to take cover again.
At the right time, from the information that was provided, those guys came, and the police arrived. They pointed those people out in the exhibit. They were all lying on the floor. The pictures of rifles were there, and the firearms. The case number was opened, the people were detained, they were given their rights, and all the firearms were put in the SCP-13.
That is when the problem started. A call was received from General Mbotho, who was still a major general, speaking to the arresting officer and asking why those people were being detained. He said those people were their officers. The arresting officer responded to him, saying no, no, General Mbotho, we went there first, this is what we found, the firearms with permits with the security. These ones are not security officers.
Then, 20 minutes later, the former head of the Hawks, General Lebeya, also called the arresting officer with the same information. The arresting officer said no, these firearms do not belong to the security company. If I just conclude, then this is what happened. Two days later, those people were released, and they were given back all those rifles. Those rifles were never subjected to ballistic testing. You do not even know whether they were involved in any crime before, but they were released.
I am showing you that there was another operation which took place where people were arrested, but because of whoever made the decisions, they decided to release them. It happened, just like in Mpumalanga, where the correctional officer was just let go.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: My question to you in relation to that investigation was whether this was an operation that you were actively involved in, or whether this is something that you have just heard about. Is this what you are saying, that you have just heard about it?
Mr Mogotsi: Yes.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: It appears to be the same with both of these investigations that you are referring to, even the one you just spoke about, where you said that General Mbotho released people who were supposed to be arrested. Mr Mogotsi: No, it is not simply heard about. That one I heard about, I made calls, I was involved. I was not on the site. Remember, when you provide information, you cannot go to the scene, in the shooting line and so forth. But in Empangeni, it was now clear that there was a defeat of the ends of justice, which case had to be opened, and because Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi decided this correctional officer should not be arrested, and I spoke to him about it, that is when I sent him the OB entry from Empangeni.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: You would note that when Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi appeared before the Committee, and I think you have just mentioned it, he expressed concern that you appear to have this kind of information available, but you are not part of the police. Do you deal with it in your statement, and do you say that the reason why Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi would think that I have dubious relationships with senior police officials is that he was not aware that I was a Crime Intelligence contact agent?
Ms James: Mr Mogotsi, I am having difficulty understanding who you actually are within SAPS. You are part of investigations. You reference in your statement “as part of my investigation”, as if you were a police officer, a detective. You also say that you sent proof of an OB entry. Number two, you also say in paragraph 40 that the correctional officer who was accused of being in possession of drugs, right? You are this detective within SAPS. Ms James: Are you aware of National Instruction 2 of 2001 that basically governs what handlers and agents are meant to do, and how operations are meant to unfold? We have been listening to you the entire morning, speaking about rates, recruitment rates. There is no such thing. There is absolutely no such thing. We are governed here. That is the point I am trying to make.

Mr Malema: You said they asked you about the tender you got from Health in Madlanga? You said they asked you about the ID and the tender.
Mr Mogotsi: Yes, and I can clarify which tender and what happened. There was a tender in the Department of Health in the North West. I did not tender. It was won by some people from outside.

They leaked the information to show how he scored and all these things. Then, going to court to interdict, we could not go to court without the appointment letter. We are supposed to say they are being appointed.
So the appointment letter could not come out in August. It came out at the end of August. So in my court papers, I said I became aware of the appointment letter in September. Now, not mentioning that we could not get the appointment letter during August, and could not go to court. As a result, that is when the evidence leader said, you lied under oath. You got the court order. It was a rule nisi application. It was granted, but you lied. You knew in August that there was a case.
Now it came as a surprise to me. Like I say, I am just a layman. Now I am saying to the evidence leader, no, we did not have the appointment letter. “You are a professional liar. You are a liar.” That is how it happened. Something that has nothing to do with the evidence.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: I know you have also mentioned, in the exhibit bundle, and we will get to that, that might probably shed further light or assist Mr Malema further in relation to the hospital tender. Mr Mogotsi: I also did not ask him a question. Remember, when you are conducting an operation of that nature, you do not ask questions that make a person doubt you. Adv Mokhoaetsi: But one thing you must do, if you are planning to use this against senior officials, or if you are making serious allegations against senior officials, one would think that you must engage and verify the facts. You must do that much so that when you come in front of a Committee like this, you can say, I have asked the relevant questions. I can substantiate the allegations that I have made. Because now, if you are not engaging, you are just believing this person's version. And you say, well, I did not want to ruin the operation. It suggests that you were not interested in whether this person might be lying to you.
Mr Mogotsi: No, as we went through this, maybe there is a big omission that I made about this whole thing. When my handler spoke to me about this witness, it was after this information, the same witness, came through Mr Cat Matlala. But I did not pay much attention to what it was, until the time when this man was organised. My interest started then to say, this is Mr Matlala. Remember, I said I was investigating all these activities and so forth. But I was so worried because I once operated with this man. And now, he had something to do with Mr Matlala. And that is how he actually had to call the colleagues to my handler. That is the omission I wanted to give.
Now, when you are dealing with the recording, you cannot ask specific questions. A person can quit. If I ask, which DNC do you prefer should do this for you? The important thing is, what is being alleged by the witness? Should I doubt him? And what am I going to achieve if I doubt his version? Remember, my job is to obtain information and give it to the relevant people. They will test it.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: No, but here you are, sitting with untested information, and making serious allegations against senior officials. So it is confusing when you say, what was he going to achieve? Here you are, and everybody is hearing you make allegations that this witness was asked to fabricate facts. And this has not been verified on your own version. You have not engaged with him, so you do not know whether he was lying to you.
Mr Mogotsi: It is not my job to know if he was lying to me. The man was a witness in the hearing. He showed me a card. I am from KZN. We have to go back again. I was with Major General Khumalo. He said this, and this, and that. What am I supposed to tell investigators about this witness? My intention at that time was to make him a tool for a witness to give a statement that there was a plot against this General. He was made to fabricate and plot against this particular General. Now, the job, we are facing that whole scenario with that intention.
Now, let me give an example. Do you know that in Madlanga, the same witness came with a statement which he provided during the day of the crime scene, of the crime busting? What the evidence leader was trying to show me was that what he wrote at that time and what he was telling me were not consistent. That is what the evidence leader was telling me. And when I looked at it, it is exactly what you are saying. But at that time, I was the one there. You are not there. No one is there. I am the one sitting with the man. I cannot tell him he is lying. He is showing me a ticket. I am from Durban. I am the witness in this matter. They are fabricating. They say it must be fabricated to have a man dismissed. Time is very short. We have to apply for the authority. Then it was granted. We did the recording.
Check those things. Because it was even verbal, it was [technical difficulties]. Once there is information, it is very raw. The information I have, I give to Colonel Schnelle. In this investigation, he is the one who goes and says, Major General, there is this matter about you. You are implicated in this way. Here is the story. Here is the recording. Not me who can do that. As I said, a contact agent cannot obtain statements. You are talking as if I were presiding over a certain matter where I had an opportunity to ask Major General Khumalo, is it true? There is no way. The man is recorded. But here is the element of the man demanding something in return. How will he get that if he does not deliver the 204, whatever we expected from him? We wanted him to be a witness. So if he was prepared to be a 204 witness, to give evidence on that, how can I doubt him? Who am I to say you are lying? It means he was going to be subjected to this testimony on his recording.
But now he is caught saying, I want this, I want this, and I want this. It is there. It is in the transcript. The only available option for him was that we also requested that he be turned into a witness against whoever was plotting with him. And indeed, as he promised me last time, remember I said, he was charged for this recording. At the same time, I think he opened the case against the people who were plotting. That
audi alteram
will only appear at the right platform, not with me.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: You said it was unfortunate that he was arrested. That is why we wanted to make sure he is protected, and his name does not appear. But more importantly, why was it so important for you not to ventilate the facts and accept this unverified information without bringing it to the attention of Major General Khumalo and General Lushaba? Why were you willing to take such a risk by accepting unverified information and coming to platforms like this with those unverified facts, instead of creating a space where, by engaging with the witness, you could verify it and allow them to have their say as well? Why were you willing to take such a risk?
Mr Mogotsi: This is very important. When the recording was done, it was never noted that, just note, this recording is going to be played in Madlanga. It is going to be played in any Committee. It is not the first time an operation of this kind has been done. You record a person, and he admits that, indeed, I said this. That is the first step. Before then, you apply. The intention is to apply and give that to the investigating officer, who has a written affidavit and has done everything. Now, it shows if he had taken steps going forward with this matter. It is his responsibility to establish the facts. At this capacity, will I speak to Major General Khumalo, come to him again and say, hey, there is this man? There was no way. The evidence, the information I have given, must then be turned into tangible evidence or anything to be used in terms of the law. Hence, it was recorded in terms of the law. That is as far as I could go.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So, in which capacity today are you sitting here and saying that the facts were fabricated, those unverified facts? In which capacity?
Mr Mogotsi: Am I sitting here?
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Yes.
Mr Mogotsi: It is not my version. You are sitting with a transcript of a record of someone who said he was approached to fabricate lies. Imagine if I did not record him, and I come here again and say there was this guy, Colonel whoever. He wanted to record; he wanted to give a statement. There was no way. What I have done so far is register the recording, apply for it to be conducted, have it recorded and submitted. Now, it is the police who, at their level, must establish the facts.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Are you not creating in your statement the impression that these facts were, in fact, fabricated? Are you not saying in your statement that General Lushaba and Major General Khumalo fabricated these facts? Is this not what you say in your statement?
Mr Mogotsi: It is based on what the man has said.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: But that would then be unverified, like I keep saying. If you say it was not your place to verify it-
Mr Mogotsi: Maybe I should give another example. Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi came here and told the Committee that Minister Senzo Mchunu and others, and that their members would brief the Committee. He spoke about the big five. He spoke about so many things. Till today, there is no link connecting Minister Senzo Mchunu, the big five, and the drug cartels. Now, I hope that if Lieutenant General Mkhwanazi comes back, you may be able to ask a similar question to him. He does not have a recording. He does not have a message from someone saying, I am selling drugs. But he was able to come here and say there is a drug cartel, the big five, and all those things. Now, I am sitting with audio, a recorded transcript, of someone who is a commissioned officer. He is a colonel by rank. I did not find this man under a tree or in a taxi rank. He is a commissioner. He is a police officer. He is saying, I am a witness in this matter. This and this and this have happened, and he did not know we were recording him. That is why we had to apply. Now, here is the evidence of this man. The questions you are asking me should be directed to this witness at the right time, unless I lie that there is a recording and transcript, and they do not exist. But they exist. It is similar to a police officer arresting someone with evidence, without an exhibit, being told by a witness that this person stole the cow. Now, you refuse to arrest this person, whereas there is a witness saying, I saw him stealing the cow. We have to arrest him and bring the witness to testify that, yes, I saw him stealing the cow. But you cannot leave it unattended to say, I need facts first. You will never get that recording again.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: I am going to leave it at that, because I think I would keep going back to the same point I am trying to make. Nobody is contesting that there was a recording with a transcript. The problem arises when we interrogate the transcript, and it appears that you were just accepting things on your own version. You were not interrogating it because you said it was not your place. Those senior officials we implicate have not had an opportunity to give us their version. You basically accept whatever this person said. I think the problem lies therein: you did not take the time to interrogate. One of the crucial things you did not interrogate is the plot, where he is talking about what happened on the day. You said, I stopped paying attention. So even then, how would we know how much you really knew? And you are relying on this to say that these people were fabricating. Do you want to elaborate on that?
Mr Mogotsi: Elaborate in what sense?

Mr Mogotsi: One of the things I did not mention: when my handler, the co-handler, arranged this DPCI matter, I got the information from my handler. So already they were talking, and that is how part of this information came to be.
And this information that Mr Matlala conveyed to my handler, somehow, that there is a person we have knowledge about. You know, information gathering is like journalism. You saw last time in Voslorus, something I used to talk about, and allow me also, Mr Malema spoke about it previously. I was so scared, and I told the police I was going to come in the morning. Passing there, there were a lot of journalists, and I did not go. I opened the case the following day. But journalists went there. They waited, thinking I was going to come, but I did not have an appointment with them.
I am trying to say, information gathering is like that. Once there is a CIT, and we hear someone has explosives, is staying in Langa, or anywhere, we are going to go there. So the moment we have someone with information, we regard that information as valuable. We take it to the relevant people. So you, evidence leader, you are making yourself, I'm the police officer, the investigating officer. I dutifully ignored asking this witness questions. My job was to record him and give it to the relevant people.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: What was your investigation on Mr Matlala? What were you investigating? You mentioned it in your statement. Maybe I should refer you to paragraphs 93 to 120. That is where you make reference to Mr Matlala, and you say that you were investigating him. What were you investigating?
Mr Mogotsi: It is similar information that there was a tender, similar to the one in Health in Mafikeng, in the North West. Mr Mogotsi: Yeah, but we never socialised, me and Mr Matlala. We never went out and had a drink or something, never.

Mr Mogotsi: We went to meet, and then I know he was too much to know about the tender. Every time, that was what he wanted.
Ms James: Mr Mogotsi, you mentioned ladies using drugs, cocaine. Can you just take us back? I didn't quite hear what you said.
Mr Mogotsi: No, I was giving an example that if you are investigating someone or wanting to get close to somebody, and you see probably night clubbing and stuff, sometimes you are able to organise people who are taking such things to be in his or her company. If he allows them to use such things in his house or wherever, you may find he is also either selling, distributing, or whoever he's living with has no problem with drugs. That's how you get close to a person. So it was just an example.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Page 83, and I'm asking this because there was a reference made to other platforms about this Impala thing. You, on page 83, asked Mr Matlala to assist you with something for the guest. And he says Impala. What does that mean?
Mr Mogotsi: Me asking him about Impala. Oh, the time in Cape Town, like this thing in Camps Bay, he did mention for me he may have some Impala meat and stuff that we can have for our guests at that time. So that's what I thought. Adv Mokhoaetsi: No, that's why I'm asking for clarity. I thought I heard Impala, and I just thought I should clarify. What does Impala mean when you ask for or organise something for the guest, and he says Impala? So it's wild meat.
Mr Mogotsi: Yeah.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: On page 91, Mr Matlala is saying here, OK, when you get back, organise a proper set-up going further, especially the main man behind all this. What is that? What does that mean? Who is the main man? And what does this mean? This is after your meeting at Houghton.
Mr Mogotsi: See, I cannot really confirm the big man, but usually, most of the time, Mr Matlala was expecting to actually meet with the Minister. He wanted so desperately to have a session with him. But I did not attend, but I think it was the Minister. He never wanted them because I once said I could arrange a chief of staff and General Sibiya, but he didn't want them. It means he refers to the Minister.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So that is what that refers to?
Mr Mogotsi: Yeah, so he's looking for the big man.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: And then on page 93, Mr Matlala is asking you whether you can go to the media about articles about Crime Intelligence information, it seems, SPLASH funds, and consumption. And this is where, I suppose, it gets confusing, where we get your statement, and you tell the Committee that you are a Crime Intelligence contact agent, and you are busy with heavy investigations with Mr Matlala, and every exchange, most of it, is in relation to investigations that you've conducted. But the only one, as I said earlier, was only in relation to the tender. That's the only investigation that's on record. Why is this exchange about Crime Intelligence? Was this part of your investigations, or what does this exchange mean? And some, when we've seen it, have been, I believe, there were charges as well, of information being made available to the public, which is considered Crime Intelligence information, and how that is viewed in a very serious light and a very serious transgression. But now we have somebody from Crime Intelligence busy exchanging this kind of information with somebody whom he is supposedly investigating. It seems really strange. Why would you exchange information? And why would you even discuss with Mr Matlala that he could possibly publish the information? And did he, in fact, publish the information?
Mr Mogotsi: But it is he who sent to me. And he asked me if he could run the story, 'My guy wants to run the story.' And then I said to him, I came on Friday. And I responded that he must say first what it is that he wanted to publish. And the answer to why we would share information? Now, you see, the information is already on a third person besides me and Mr Matlala, that he wanted to share. And this information, as to, you're talking about the Crime Intelligence officers and them, who cannot disclose this information and so forth. And you ask me, you see, I'm not a Crime Intelligence officer.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: So you don't prescribe to the protocol that's applicable to them?
Mr Mogotsi: It's not that you prescribe or you don't prescribe. Now, perhaps this should be clarified. Here is the information in front of me. And if even the Committee, including Madlanga, where the information is brought before the Committee, the same Committee which has so much power, to some, to even someone, the IGI or whoever, to deal with this, it means the Committee is not going to get any truth. We are investigating the allegations as the Committee. You'll never get the truth because whoever is doing anything wrong is doing it knowingly. It cannot be used against him because it is classified. Now, there comes information to people like us. It gets out there, and it is presented here. Now, people get charged. It means the truth will never come out. Hence, I asked, if possible, if the Committee could summon, including the suspended Inspector General of Intelligence. He has the power to, because he has the report, this IGI report. Maybe the Committee may have access to it and look into it. Now, the truth is that whatever information we give you comes in bits and pieces. It means it will never work.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: Do you see how you're asking the Committee to come and help you in relation to Crime Intelligence or allegations against Crime Intelligence, and possibly investigate that further to see if those people should be charged? That's essentially what you're asking the Committee, no? What are you asking the Committee to do?
Mr Mogotsi: No, I'm asking the Committee to meet with the IGI, with the information. The Committee gets the prosecuting authority and says, is this prosecutable or not?
Adv Mokhoaetsi: But it should be investigated, isn't it?
Mr Mogotsi: The IGI has investigated. In the IGI, there is a finding of the IGI. Again, if a property has been bought with state money, here's the title deed, and it's registered in the name of an individual. Now, we have to declassify it before, or there's no commission of crime committed.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: But you see, and I don't want to go back to it, but you see the difficulty that I've raised earlier about you coming to the Committee and asking for classified information to be declassified, and the exchange of classified information in WhatsApp texts between yourself and Mr Matlala, but you're not willing at all to give anything to this Committee in relation to what you've done so far as Mr Matlala is concerned.
Mr Mogotsi: It's not that I don't want to give. We have given you, it is you, the evidence leader, who had to hide that information, the evidence, the only evidence I told you. This is the only evidence I have that the property was bought as a title deed, and this is the amount. Because it's classified, we understand. So, like in the case of that informant who was killed, I know who the handler was, and I know the investigating officer who investigated the murder, and I know the commander of the handler. It can be corroborated 100%. And then with this one, the property, here it is, then you get whoever must lead the prosecution for the prosecution of these people.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: I think we're talking past each other, but I was trying to say that information is put in front of the Committee. Be it redacted, yes, we know that, but the Committee will know where to find it. But what the Committee won't know where to find is your investigations in relation to Mr Matlala.
Mr Mogotsi: Yeah, but Chairperson, it seems like I have promised that there is something that we got against Mr Matlala, and he is about to be arrested and so forth. If there is an investigation, depending on where it is, there are people, there are state institutions that are investigating Mr Matlala. It's not that from me you can obtain any written statement or anything written. I've said that because once the Committee can call us to do that, it's when I'm going to involve my handler, who will involve his structures, the institutions commander going up on how to deal with the Committee on the information.
Adv Mokhoaetsi: There's a reason why I keep going back there. And you, on your own version, have also confirmed that there seem to be links, there seem to be the people that you've referred to in your statement, that you were assisting, are also people that are known to Mr Matlala.
